Therefore, it is proper to conclude that the consciousness of 'I', which has nothing to contradict it, has really the self for its object; 
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तस्मादहमिति मतिर्बाधकापेता साक्षादात्मगोचरैव ।
</details>


<details><summary>तिरु-नाङ्गूर्-अण्णङ्गरार्यः</summary>

**तस्माद्** इति । अबाधिताहम्-बुद्धिर् मुख्याऽत्म-गोचरैव । देहादौ तु सा भ्रान्ति-लक्षणैवेति भावः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अन्-आत्मनि तु शरीरे भवन्ती अविद्येति युक्तम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

and that, on the other hand, the consciousness of 'I' which arises in regard to the body that is not the soul, is ignorance. 
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनात्मनि तु शरीरे भवन्ती अविद्येति युक्तम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

उक्तम् च — "श्रूयताम् चाप्य् अविद्यायाः स्वरूपम् कुल-नन्दन । अन्-आत्मन्य् आत्म-बुद्धिर् या" इति महर्षिणा वासिष्ठ-नन्दनेन ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(In agreement with this) it has been said by (Parāśara) the grandson of Vasistha: 'O thou! the giver of delight to thy family! Hear from me the essential nature of ignorance; it is the consideration of the not-self as the self.'[F56_97] 

[F56_97]: *Visnu* Purāna. VI. vii. 10.

</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

उक्तं चऽश्रूयतां चाप्यविद्यायाः स्वरूपं कुलनन्दन । अनात्मन्यात्मबुद्धिर्याऽ इति महर्षिणा वासिष्ठनन्दनेन ।
</details>


<details><summary>तिरु-नाङ्गूर्-अण्णङ्गरार्यः</summary>

अत्र संवादि-पुराण-रत्न-वचनं **श्रूयताम्** इति । **आत्मन्य् एष न दोषाय शब्दो ऽहम् इति यो द्विज । अनात्मन्य् आत्म-विज्ञानं शब्दो वा भ्रान्ति-लक्षणः** ॥ इति च तत्रत्यम् अत्रानुसन्धेयम् । आत्म-विज्ञानम् अहम्-बुद्धिः । शब्दो ऽहं-शब्दः । वासिष्ठ-नन्दनेन वसिष्ठ-पुत्रस्य शक्तेः पुत्रेण भगवता पराशरेण ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च ज्ञप्ति-मात्र-प्रतिभासः कस्यचिच् शरीरे ऽस्ति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(Our position squares well with Parāśara's definition of ignorance; but yours does not; for,) the illusory apprehension of the body as pure consciousness occurs to no one. 
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच ज्ञप्तिमात्र प्रतिभासः कस्यचित्शरीरेऽस्ति ।
</details>


<details><summary>तिरु-नाङ्गूर्-अण्णङ्गरार्यः</summary>

देहात्मभ्रमाकारपरीक्षातो ऽपि स्वीकार्यम् अहम्-अर्थत्वम् आत्मनः इत्य् आह **न च ज्ञप्ती**ति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

येन [[तन्मात्रात्मवादिनोऽप्यनात्म (न्योत्म) बुद्धिरुपपद्येत|तन्-मात्रात्म-वादिनो ऽप्य् अन्-आत्मन्यात्म-बुद्धिर् उपपद्येत]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even to you, who maintain that pure consciousness alone is self, the consideration of the non-soul as the self will be possible, if there is the illusory apprehension of the body as pure consciousness. 
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

येन तन्मात्रात्मवादिनोऽप्यनात्म (न्योत्म) बुद्धिरुपपद्येत ।
</details>


<details><summary>तिरु-नाङ्गूर्-अण्णङ्गरार्यः</summary>

अनात्म-बुद्धिः अनात्मन्य् आत्म-बुद्धिः । तथैव पाठः स्याद् इति सम्भाव्यते । ज्ञप्ति-मात्रस्यात्मत्वे स्थूला संविद् इत्य् एव देहात्मभ्रमस्याऽकारः स्यात् । न तु स्थूलो ऽहमिति । अतो ऽप्य् आत्माहमर्थ एव । यस्मिन् सति अहम् इति बुद्धिर् देहे उदेति । अपक्रान्ते च न । सो ऽयम् आत्माहमर्थ एवेति च युक्तम् अभ्युपगन्तुम् इति भावः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

१.१४ अतः प्रत्यक्ष-सिद्धत्वाद् उक्त-न्यायागमान्वयात् ।  
अविद्या-योगतश् चात्मा [[ज्ञाताऽहमिति|ज्ञाताहम् इति]] भासते ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

As is proved by perception (the judgment 'I know' establishes knowledge to be an attribute and the 'I' to be its possessor), and as it results from the application of the aforesaid reasons (such as, if pure consciousness alone persisted and the 'I' disappeared in the state of release, no one would strive for realisation), and as scriptural texts (declare that even released souls refer to themselves as 'I'), and as there is the possibility of ignorance (only on our position), it follows that the self which is the knower presents itself as the 'I'.

</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

1.14 अतः प्रत्यक्षसिद्धत्वादुक्तन्यायागमान्वयात् ।  
अविद्यायोगतश्चात्मा ज्ञाताऽहमिति भासते ॥
</details>


<details><summary>तिरु-नाङ्गूर्-अण्णङ्गरार्यः</summary>

अहम्-अर्थस्याऽत्मत्वं निगमयति **अत** इति । जानाम्य् अहम् इति ज्ञान-धर्मित्वेन प्रत्यक्ष-सिद्धत्वाद् अहम्-अर्थस्यैवाऽत्मत्वम् । अहन्त्वेन तस्य मुक्ताव् अपि भाने ऽनुमानम् उक्तम् आगमश् च । प्रत्यक्त्वान्यथानुपपत्ति-लक्षणस् तर्को ऽप्य् उक्तः आत्मनो ऽहम्-अर्थत्व-व्यवस्थापकः । स्थूलो ऽहमिति देहात्मभ्रमरूपाविद्या-सङ्गतेश् च ज्ञाताहमर्थ एवात्मा, स च सर्वदाहमिति भासते इति कारिकार्थः । आत्मा ज्ञातैवेत्य् अत्रापि प्रत्यक्षादिकम् अस्तीति गर्भितम् अत्र । प्रत्यक्षं चाहं जानामीत्यादिकं प्रसिद्धम् एव । ज्ञानस्य देहादि-धर्मत्व-निषेधेन परिशेषानुमानम् अपि सिद्धम् । सास्त्रवचनानि च अग्रे मूल एव निर्देक्ष्यन्ते । ज्ञान-समानाश्रयत्वाद् अज्ञानस्याज्ञातृत्वे आत्मनो ऽविद्यान्वयायोग इति तर्को ऽप्यक्त-प्राय इति । एवं ज्ञातुर अहम्-अर्थस्यात्मत्वं व्यवास्थापि ॥ १४ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

इति ज्ञातुर् आत्मनो [[मुक्त्यादौ|मुक्त्य्-आदौ]] सर्वदाप्य् अहम्-भाव-भान-समर्थन-प्रकरणम् ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Thus ends the section supporting the manifestation of the 'I' in the case of the self as the knower, in liberation and at all other times.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

इति ज्ञातुरात्मनो मुक्त्यादौ सर्वदाप्यहम्भावभानसमर्थनप्रकरणम्॥
</details>

## अजडत्वान् न

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यद्-उक्तम् अजडत्वाद् वित्तिर् एवाऽत्मेति; तत्रेदं वाच्यं किम् इदम् अजडत्वं नामेति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

With regard to (your) assertion that consciousness itself is the self because it (consciousness) is not non-intelligent, it has to be pointed out (that you must explain) what you understand by 'not non-intelligence'.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदुक्तमजडत्वाद्वित्तिरेवाऽत्मेति; तत्रेदं वाच्यं किमिदमजडत्वं नामेति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[यद्युच्येतेति;|यद्य् उच्येत —]] [[सदपि|सद् अपि]] [[यन्न|यन् न]] प्रकाशते [[तज्जडम्|तज् जडम्]], तद्-विपरीतम् अव्यभिचरित-प्रकाश-सत्ताकम् अजडम् इति; तथा सति सुखादिभिर् व्यभिचारी हेतुः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it is replied that a non-intelligent entity is that which may (at times) fail to manifest itself, even though it be existent, and that an intelligent entity is that which has an opposite nature, namely, an existence invariably associated with manifestation (we point out that) since pleasure and the like are not considered to be soul even though they are not non-intelligent your reason is fallacious.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यद्युच्येतेति; सदपि यन्न प्रकाशते तज्जडम्, तद्विपरीतमव्यभिचरितप्रकाशसत्ताकमजडमिति; तथा सति सुखादिभिर्व्यभिचारी हेतुः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न खलु सुख-दुःखेच्छादयो विद्यमाना अपि [[कदाचिदमवभासमाना|कदाचिद् अनवभासमाना]] भवन्ति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Indeed, when pleasure, pain, desire and the like exist at all they never fail to present themselves.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न खलु सुखदुःखेच्छादयो विद्यमाना अपि कदाचिदमवभासमाना  भवन्ति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

स्व-सत्ता-प्रयुक्त-प्रकाशत्वम् अपि दीपादिभिर् अनैकान्तिकम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(If an intelligent entity is defined as) that which depends for its manifestation on its own existence, (we point out that) since the lamp and the like are not taken to be the soul even though they depend for their manifestation on their own existence, your reason is fallacious.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

स्वसत्ताप्रयुक्तप्रकाशत्वमपि दीपादिभिरनैकान्तिकम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ज्ञान-व्यतिरिक्त-प्रकाशानङ्गीकाराच् चासिद्धता, विरुद्धता च ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, as a manifestation different from consciousness is not admitted (by you) your hetu (reason), namely, intelligence occurring in the argument that consciousness itself is the soul, because it is intelligent) becomes unestablished (i. e. commits the fallacy of svarūpāsiddha); it also contradicts your theory (that consciousness is attributeless).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ज्ञानव्यतिरिक्तप्रकाशानङ्गीकाराच्चासिद्धता, विरुद्धता च ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यदि मतम् अव्यभिचरित-प्रकाशो ऽपि सुखादिर् अन्यस्मै प्रकाशत इति घट इव जडतां नातिवर्तते, तेनानात्मेति; ज्ञानं वा किं स्वस्मै प्रकाशते?
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it is your view that pleasure and the like, although invariably associated with manifestation, are bound to be non-intelligent, for the reason that, like the pot, they manifest themselves for the sake of others, and are in consequence, to be considered as not-soul, (we ask in reply,) Do you mean then to suggest that knowledge too manifests itself for the sake of something other than itself, namely, the knower, the 'I'?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदि मतमव्यभिचरितप्रकाशोऽपि सुखादिरन्यस्मै प्रकाशत इति घट इव जडतां नातिवर्तते, तेनानात्मेति; ज्ञानं वा किं स्वस्मै प्रकाशते?
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अन्यस्यैव हि तद् अपि जानतो ऽहम्-अर्थस्य प्रथते ऽहं जानामीति, अहम्-सुखीति-वत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The judgment 'I know' establishes this, even as the judgment 'I am having pleasure' (proves that pleasure presents itself for the sake of the 'I').
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अन्यस्यैव हि तदपि जानतोऽहमर्थस्य प्रथतेऽहं जानामीति, अहं सुखीतिवत् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तेन स्वस्मै प्रकाशमानत्वम् अभिप्रेत्य प्रयुज्यमानो ऽजडत्व-हेतुरसिद्धः संविदि ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Therefore, the quality of being not non-intelligent (ajaḍatva), taken in the sense of the quality of manifesting for one's own sake, does not exist (asiddha) in consciousness (which is the minor term or paksa in your argument).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तेनस्वस्मै प्रकाशमानत्वमभिप्रेत्य प्रयुज्यमानोऽजडत्वहेतुरसिद्धः संविदि ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अतः सत्तयैव स्वम् आत्मानं प्रति सिध्यन् अजडो ऽहम्-अर्थ एवात्मा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Hence, it is only the entity known as 'I', which is not non-intelligent, and which manifests itself for its own sake by its own existence that constitutes the self.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अतः सत्तयैव स्वमात्मानं प्रति सिध्यन्नजडोऽहमर्थ एवात्मा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तत्-सम्बन्धायत्ता तु ज्ञानस्यापि प्रकाशता ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P58]] The luminosity of consciousness itself is dependent on its connection with the self.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तत्सम्बन्धायत्ता तु ज्ञानस्यापि प्रकाशता ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अत एव हि स्वाश्रय-चेतनं प्रति प्रकटता, इतरं प्रत्य् अप्रकटता च ज्ञानस्य सुख-दुःखादेर् इव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That is why knowledge, as in the case of pleasure, pain and the like, manifests itself to that intelligent person who is its own substrate, and not to anybody else.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अत एव हि स्वाश्रयचेतनं प्रति प्रकटता, इतरं प्रत्यप्रकटता च ज्ञानस्य सुखदुःखदेरिव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च एवम् आत्मान्तर-सम्बन्धम् अर्थान्तरं वापेक्ष्यायम् आत्मा ऽत्मने प्रकाशते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The self, on the contrary, does not present itself for its own sake by depending on its connection with some other soul or some other entity.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नचैवमात्मान्तरसम्बन्धमर्थान्तरं वापेक्ष्यायमात्माऽत्मने प्रकाशते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एतच् चानन्तरम् एवोपपादयिष्यते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

This will be explained presently.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एतच्चानन्तरमेवोपपादयिष्यते ।
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

इति ज्ञानात्मत्व-साधकाजडत्व-दूषणम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The unsoundness of the argument that consciousness itself is the soul as it is insentient
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

इति ज्ञानात्मत्वसाधकाजडत्वदूषणम्
</details>

### ग्राह्य-ग्राहक-विकल्प--प्रत्युद्धार-निराकरणम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The argument that on account of the invariable concomitance of the knowledge of 'I' and consciousness they are identical is unsound—
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च ज्ञानेन सहोपलम्भ-नियमो ऽहम्-अर्थस्यार्थान्तरतां वारयति, ज्ञानस्यापि तथात्व-प्रसङ्गात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

You cannot maintain that the invariable association of the manifestation of 'I' with consciousness prevents us from taking the 'I' to be a distinct entity; for, on the same count, it might as well follow that consciousness itself cannot be taken to be a distinct entity.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न च ज्ञानेन सहोपलम्भनियमोऽहमर्थस्यार्थान्तरतां वारयति, ज्ञानस्यापि तथात्वप्रसङ्गात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तद् अपि हि तेन नियतेन सहोपलम्भम् इत्य् अहम्-अर्थाद् अनर्थान्तरं मिथ्या-रूपम् एवाऽपद्येत ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Since it (consciousness) invariably manifests itself along with the 'I', it would follow that consciousness also is not an entity different from 'I' and that it is unreal.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तदपि हि तेन नियतेन सहोपलम्भमित्यहमर्थादनर्थान्तरं मिथ्यारूपमेवाऽपद्येत ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

असिद्धश् च संविद्-विशेषैः सहोपलम्भ-नियमः, प्रत्येकं व्यभिचार-दर्शनात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Moreover, since in each item of knowledge we meet with the absence of the invariable association of the manifestation of 'I', the invariable manifestation of 'I' with any particular item of knowledge does not exist.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

असिद्धश्च संविद्विशेषैः सहोपलम्भनियमः, प्रत्येकं व्यभिचारदर्शनात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च विशेष-मात्रं निर्धूत-निखिल-विषय-विशेषोपश्लेषं वा वित्ति-मात्रम् अस्ति, येन सहोपलम्भ-नियमः संवेदितुर् अभिधीयेत ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, there is neither an object (viṣaya) apart (from its knowledge) nor pure knowledge divested of any relation to all particular objects; if either existed, then the invariable concomitance of the manifestation of knower with knowledge could be posited.[^58_98]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^58_98]: Having pointed out that the sahopalambhaniyama itself is impossible for the reason that there is the presentation of the 'I' even in the absence of any particular item of knowledge, Yamunācārya proceeds to establish the defective nature of the illustrative example, which the opponent must cite in his argument, namely. wherever there is invariable apprehension of two things together there'must be non-difference between them, as in the case of knowledge and its object. In order to prove that knowledge and its vişaya are non-different, the object by itself and the knowledge by itself must be taken and shown to be invariably concomitant. But, in truth, neither exists apart from the other. Hence, the illustrative example is subject to the charge of being unproven.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न च विशेषमात्रं निर्धूतनिखिलविषयविशेषोपश्लेषं वा वित्तिमात्रमस्ति, येन सहोपलम्भनियमः संवेदितुरभिधीयेत ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

सामान्यं तु सद् अपि सौगतैर् न वस्तुतया ऽस्थीयते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P59]] And even if the property common to all knowledge (jñānasāmānya) is existent, it is not considered to be a positive entity by the Buddhists.[^59_99]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^59_99]: The Buddhists cannot hope to escape the difficulty by saying that between vişayatva (the property of being an object of knowledge) and jñanatva (the property common to all knowledge) there is invariable concomitance, for they do not consider sāmānya (universal) to be a positive entity. Its admission, they say, leads to all sorts of absurdities. The universal is, at best, a working fiction, a useful device in thinking. When certain things are regarded as similar, it is not in virtue of their possessing some common features, but because of their distinction from the rest. The perception of a cow, for example, does not indicate that cowness, as a positive quality. exists in that creature; it only signifies that it is different from all non-cows (*apoha*) See Six *Buddhist Nyaya Tracts*.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सामान्यं तु सदपि सौगतेर्न वस्तुतयाऽस्थीयते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

समस्त-वृत्ति-प्रत्यस्तमये ऽपि स्वयञ्ज्योतिर् अयम् आत्मा वतिष्ठत इति च वक्ष्यामः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

We shall show that even in the absence of all (knowledge due to mental) modifications, the soul exists as a self-luminous entity.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

समस्तवृत्तिप्रत्यस्तमयेऽपि स्वयञ्ज्योतिरयमात्मावतिष्ठत इति च वक्ष्यामः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[स्ववाग्विघातश्चएकं|स्व-वाग्-विघातश् च एकं]] द्वाव् इति निर्देशात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

From the assertion that the two (i. e., knowledge and knower) are one, there arises a contradiction in the opponent's own statement;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

स्ववाग्विघातश्चएकं द्वाविति निर्देशात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

द्वयोर् हि ह्य् एक-क्रियानुप्रवेशे सह-शब्दः, शिष्येण सह गच्छत्य् आचार्य इति यथा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

for, the word saha (with) is used only when two entities enter on an identical course of action, as in the instance 'with the pupil, the preceptor comes'.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

द्वयोर्ह्येकक्रियानुप्रवेशे सहशब्दः, शिष्येण सह गच्छत्याचार्य इति यथा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अपि च [[निलतद्धियोरिति|नील-तद्धियोर् इति]] द्वे उपादाय अभेद इत्य् एकत्व-विधिः सवित्री-वन्ध्यात्व-विधिर् इव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Further, after referring to the two (i. e. blue and its awareness) by the expression *nila-taddhiyoḥ* to assert (their) identity by the word abhedaḥ (non-difference)[^59_100] is like stating that one's mother is a barren woman.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^59_100]: The reference here is to the Buddhistic dictum-sahopalambhaniyamada- bhedo nilataddhiyoḥ.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अपि च निलतद्धियोरिति द्वे उपादाय अभेद इत्येकत्वविधिः सवित्रीवन्ध्यात्वविधिर् इव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अनेकान्तश् च संविदि प्रतिषिध्यमानैर् जडत्वादिभिः; सर्वज्ञ-ज्ञानेन सहोपलम्भ-नियम-भागिभिः संसारि-ज्ञानैश् च ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, in view of the fact that qualities such as non-intelligence and the like are denied to consciousness, and in view of the fact that the knowledge of the soul in bondage is invariably apprehended along with the all-embracing knowledge of the omniscient being (sarvajña) (your hetu) is liable to be charged with *anekanta* dosa.[^59_101]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^59_101]: By drawing attention to the fact that the hetu (sahopalambhaniyama) is present even in cases where the sadhya (non-difference) is not known to exist, Yamunarya exposes the fallacy (i. e. *anekānta*) vitiating the argument of the opponent. The latter may try to meet this by admitting that even in those cases the sadhya is really present. In reply to this, Yamuna says in the next sentence that this admission leads to absurdities.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनेकान्तश्च संविदि प्रतिषिध्यमानैर्जडत्वादिभिः; सर्वज्ञज्ञानेन सहोपलम्भनियमभागिभिः संसारिज्ञानैश्च ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तेषाम् अभेदाभ्युपगमे ज्ञानस्य जडत्व-मूर्तत्वादि, बुद्धस्य बद्धत्वम् इत्य् आपद्येत ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P60]] If, in their case (i. e., between the knowledge of the soul in bondage and that of the sarvajña), non-difference is admitted, the quality of non-intelligence and that of having a form and the like would have to be ascribed to consciousness, and the quality of being a bound soul would have to be attributed to the Buddha.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तेषामभेदाभ्युपगमे ज्ञानस्य जडत्वमूर्तत्वादि, बुद्धस्य बद्धत्वमित्यापद्येत ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Even the contention that since one and the same consciousness presents the invariable concomitance of knower known and knowledge they are identical is refuted-
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

नियमनैक-ज्ञान-सिद्धत्वम् अप्य् उक्त-प्रकारेण [[प्रत्यु क्तम्|प्रत्युक्तम्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

As shown before, even the contention of their (knowledge and knower) being invariably the objects (visaya) of one and the same knowledge stands condemned.[^60_102]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^60_102]: To obviate the contradiction involved in sahopalambhaniyama to which attention of the opponent was drawn, he shifts his ground and employs a different hetu, namely, *niyamena* ekajnānasiddhatvam.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नियमेनैकज्ञानसिद्धत्वमप्युक्तप्रकारेण प्रत्यु क्तम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

विपक्ष-व्यतिरेकश् चासिद्धः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, here the non-existence of the hetu in cases where the sadhya is known to be absent (vipakṣa) cannot be established;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

विपक्षव्यतिरेकश्चासिद्धः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

भवतु नियमनैक-ज्ञान-सिद्धत्वं ज्ञान-ज्ञेय-ज्ञातृणाम्, मा च भूद् अभेदः; को विरोधः? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

for there may be the invariable presentation of knowledge, the known and the knower in one and the same knowledge, and still there may not be non-difference between them.[^60_103] What is the inconsistency here?
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^60_103]: The opponent argues that knowledge and the knower must be identical; for they are invariably apprehended together in one and the same knowledge. Against the possible objection they may be so apprehended and still may not be identical, he must adduce the indirect proof (tarka) that if they were not identical, they could not be apprehended together in the self-same knowledge. It is shown here that he is unable to do so.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

भवतु नियमेनैकज्ञानसिद्धत्वं ज्ञानज्ञेयज्ञातृणाम्, मा च भूदभेदः; को विरोधः? ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

1.15 किम् अप्रकाश-रूपत्वात् प्रकाशम् अनुरुध्यते ।  
व्यवहाराय नीलादिर् आहोस्वित् तद्-अभेदतः ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

1.15 Do (objects of knowledge, such as) blue and the like depend for their apprehension and consideration on knowledge either because they are not self-luminous or because of their non-difference (from knowledge)?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

1.15 किमप्रकाशरूपत्वात् प्रकाशमनुरुध्यते ।  
व्यवहाराय नीलादिराहोस्वित्तदभेदतः ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

1.16 इति सन्दिह्यमानत्वान् नाभेदः शक्य-निर्णयः ।  
बोध्यस्थश् चैष नियमो न पुनर् बुद्धि-बोद्धृ-गः ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

1.16 As, in this manner, it becomes a matter for doubt, it is impossible to determine that there is this non-difference. And this generalisation (that everything depends for its manifestation on consciousness) obtains only in the case of objects known and not in that of knowledge or the knower.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

1.16 इति सन्दिह्यमानत्वान्नाभेदः शक्यनिर्णयः ।  
बोध्यस्थश्चैष नियमो न पुनर्बुद्धिबोद्धृगः ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

स्पष्टश् च प्रत्यक्ष-बाधः, सर्व-ज्ञानेषु वेद्याद् इव वित्तेर् अपि वेदितुर् भेदस्यापरोक्षत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, the conflict (of this theory) with perceptual experience is obvious; for, in every knowledge, the distinction of the knower from knowledge is apprehended.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

स्पष्टश्च प्रत्यक्षबाधः, सर्वज्ञानेषु वेद्यादिव वित्तेरपि वेदितुर्भेदस्यापरोक्षत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च प्रतियोगिनः प्रत्यक्षत्वं दृश्यत्वं वा भेदस्याऽपरोक्ष्ये त्व् अपेक्षितव्यम्, सिद्धि-मात्रेण तद्-उपपत्ताव् अप्रयोजकत्वेन तद्-विशेषस्यानाक्षेपात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(At this stage the opponent may object and say that the distinction of knower from knowledge cannot be perceived, since the counter-correlative (i. e., knowledge) is not perceived; and that even if it is admitted to be perceptible on the strength of the doctrine of svayamprakāśatva, it does not help, since it is not visible. To this we reply) in the matter of the perception of difference there is no necessity for the counter-correlative (*pratiyogi*) to be either perceptible or visible; for when the direct perception of difference is possible with the aid of the mere thought of the counter-correlative, a particular variety of this knowledge is not required, in as much as it is not responsible (for the perception of difference).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच प्रतियोगिनः प्रत्यक्षत्वं दृश्यत्वं वा भेदस्याऽपरोक्ष्ये त्वपेक्षितव्यम्, सिद्धिमात्रेण तदुपपत्तावप्रयोजकत्वेन तद्वविशेषस्यानाक्षेपात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अनवभासमाने ऽपि प्रतियोगिनि भावाः स्वरूपत एव विलक्षणाः प्रत्यक्ष्यन्त इति सर्व-लोक-स्व-साक्षिकम् एतत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P61]] (We may go a step further and say that) even when the counter-correlative is not apprehended, things are directly perceived as being distinct in themselves;[^61_104] and this will be testified to by everybody from his own experience.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^61_104]: The apprehension of the generic property (jati) of a thing, say a pot, is nothing more than the apprehension of the distinction from other things, i.e., non-pots; and it prevents erroneous identifications. In fact, difference (bheda) is nothing more than generic property (jāti). To grasp the generic property in itself it is unnecessary that the counter-correlative (pratiyogi) should have been perceived. But the generic property, in its aspect of eliminating erroneous identifications is known as bheda (difference), and is, certainly, found to pre-suppose knowledge of the pratiyogi. See *Sri Bhasya*, Ananda Press edn. p. 29; see also verses 13-14 of Adravyasara in *Tattvamuktākalāpa* and *Sarvārthasiddhi* 'yadā punaḥ adhyāsa nivartakatvarūpadharmāntaravaišistyena vyavahriyante, tada bheda iti usyante | tena tesameva dharmāņām vastusvarūpeņa vyavahriamāṇādmļne pratiyogisā pekṣatvam | adhyasanivartakatvarūpadharmantaravaisiṣṭyena vyavabriyamāņānām pratiyogisa pekşatvam iti |
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनवभासमानेऽपि प्रतियोगिनि भावाः स्वरूपत एव विलक्षणाः प्रत्यक्ष्यन्त इति सर्वलोकस्वसाक्षिकमेतत् ।
</details>

### प्रवाहसन्ततिः
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The contention that knower and known are one on ground of invariable concomitance even as different flames are considered one on account of similarity-
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ननु जीवतो भेद-प्रत्यक्षस्य शिरसि पद-निधानेन सहोपलम्भ-नियमस्याभेदेन प्रतिबन्ध-ग्रहणम् इति कथमिव ततस् तद्-बाध-सम्भवः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(The opponent may ask) since, by trampling on the head of the perception of difference which is alive, (we) notice the universal concomitance between the invariable manifestation (of two things) together and their non-difference, how can the sublation of non-difference be effected by perception of difference?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ननु जीवतो भेदप्रत्यक्षस्य शिरसि पदनिधानेन सहोपलम्भनियमस्याभेदेन प्रतिबन्धग्रहणमिति कथमिव ततस्तद्वाधसम्भवः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा सति हि ज्वाला-भेदानुमानम् अपि तद्-एकत्व-प्रत्यभिज्ञयापोद्येत ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

If it could be effected, even the inference regarding the difference of the flames (at successive moments) would be stultified by the recognition of their identity.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथासति हि ज्वालाभेदानुमानमपि तदेकत्वप्रत्यभिज्ञयापोद्येत ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अविशेष-ज्ञो देवानां प्रियः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(The reply is that) the fool (of an opponent) is ignorant of the distinction (between these two cases).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अविशेषज्ञो देवानां प्रियः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तत्र हि [[क्ल्प्तकारणदोषानुवृत्तौ|क्लृप्त-कारण-दोषानुवृत्तौ]] सत्यां जायमानो ऽपरोक्षावभासो न निरवद्य-प्रत्यक्ष-पूर्वकम् अनुमानं बाधितुम् अर्हति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P62]] Indeed in the case of the flame, the perceptual knowledge, which arises when there is continuity of the defects in the settled causes (of knowledge) is capable of sublating the inference which is based upon defectless perception.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तत्र हि क्ल्प्तकारणदोषानुवृत्तौ सत्यां जायमानोऽपरोक्षावभासो न निरवद्यप्रत्यक्षपूर्वकमनुमानं बाधितुमर्हति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा हि — [[तथाहिअचिरनिर्वापितारोपितेष्वेकवर्तिभागवर्तिषु|अचिर-निर्वापितारोपितेष्व् एक-वर्ति-भाग-वर्तिषु]] [[बहुषुदीपेषु|बहुषु दीपेषु]] तद्-भेदादर्शिनः सुसदृशतया स एवायम् इति स्मृतिर् उपजायते इति दृष्टम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

To make the point clear-it is found that, on account of close similarity between the different flames that are extinguished and lighted immediately after and which exist in the parts of one and the same which the remembrance "This is, certainly, that flame which I saw before" occurs to one who has not noticed their difference.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिअचिरनिर्वापितारोपितेष्वेकवर्तिभागवर्तिषु बहुषुदीपेषु तद्भेदादर्शिनः सुसदृशतया स एवायमिति स्मृतिरुपजायते इति दृष्टम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The example of different terms appearing as identical is not helpful-
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अतो ऽन्यत्राप्य् अप्रतिबन्ध-पुष्कल-कारण-क्रमोपनिपाताद् अवयव-विश्लेषाच् च सुसदृश-निरन्तर-प्रवृत्त-प्रदीप-प्रवाहाळम्बनैव तथा मतिर् इति निश्चीयते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Therefore, even in other cases (where the flames are not extinguished and kindled afresh), as there is the occurrence of a series of the complete set of causal factors, which have no counter-acting circumstances, and as there is the separation of parts (of the causal conditions) it is to be concluded that such a knowledge (of identity) has for its object closely similar and incessantly flowing flame-series.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अतोऽन्यत्राप्य्अप्रतिबन्धपुष्कलकारणक्रमोपनिपातादवयवविश्लेषाच्च सुसदृशनिरन्तरप्रवृत्तप्रदीपप्रवाहालम्बनैव तथा मतिरिति निश्चीयते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथैक-नानात्व-प्रत्ययः स्वतः-प्राप्तेन्द्रिय-वृत्ति-विपर्यय-प्रयुक्तः सम-समयोपजायमानानेकानवद्य-प्रत्यक्ष-प्रतिक्षिप्त-[[विषयश्चद्विचन्द्रादौ|विषयश् च द्विचन्द्रादौ]] दृष्ट इति नासौ तत्रैकत्वानुमानम् अभिभवितुं प्रभवति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Similarly, as the cognition of diversity in regard to one and the same thing is found in the case of seeing the moon double and the like as being occasioned by the swerving from the normal mode of the working of the sense-organ,[^62_105] and as having its object contradicted by the simultaneously arising defectless cognitions of many persons, this (perception of diversity) is not capable of setting aside the inference of identity in those cases.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^62_105]: Either through pressure of the finger upon the eye or on account of some defect in the visual mechanism, the rays of the organ of sight (nayanarasmi) split and travel in two directions, thereby creating, for all practical purposes, two mutually independent apparatuses of vision. One apparatus apprehends the moon in her proper place, without, however, apprehending her unity; the other, which moves somewhat obliquely, apprehends, at first, a place close by the moon, and subsequently the moon herself, without, however, noticing the intervening space separating this place and the moon. These two perceptions-one manifesting the moon in her proper place, and other in a place close by-arise in such quick succession that the perceiver fails to notice the order of their occurrence, and thereby omits to note their varying natures. Thus, the double apparatus causes two apprehensions; and as the apprehensions differ, there is also difference in the character of the object apprehended. The mistake here lies in the failure to notice the fact that the duality found in the places is unrelated to the moon. Hence, the perception of two moons. The Prabhakara account, which is closely similar to this, would, however, say that the double apparatus yields a duality of apprehensions, but it fails to grasp that the duality present in the apprehensions is unrelated to the moon. Compare: 'netravṛttih vittigatadvitvam candrañca agrhitabhedam gṛhṇātiti Prabhakarah | yathā
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथैकनानात्वप्रत्ययः स्वतःप्राप्तेन्द्रियवृत्तिविपर्ययप्रयुक्तः समसमयोपजायमानानेकानवद्यप्रत्यक्षप्रतिक्षिप्तविषयश्चद्विचन्द्रादौ दृष्ट इति नासौ तत्रैकत्वानुमानमभिभवितुं प्रभवति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न चैवम् इह ज्ञातृ-ज्ञान-ज्ञेय-विवेक-साक्षात्कारी प्रत्यय इति प्रतिरुन्धद्ध्य् एवायम् इहाभेदानुमानोदय-प्रसक्तिम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

But here, the knowledge which immediately apprehends the distinction of the knower, knowledge and the known is not of such a nature; hence, here it certainly does prevent the very possibility of the birth of the inference of identity.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न चैवमिह ज्ञातृज्ञानज्ञेयविवेकसाक्षात्कारी प्रत्यय इति प्रतिरुणद्ध्येवायमिहाभेदानुमानोदयप्रसक्तिम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न चोपलब्धि-साहित्य-नियमाद् एव तथात्वम् अत्रानुमेयम् इति युक्तम्, विपक्षे बाधकानुपलब्धेः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P63]] But, here it is not proper to say that identity is inferable on the mere basis of the invariable manifestation of two things together;[^63_106] for we know of no obstacle preventing the existence of this hetu *(probans)* in cases where the sadhya (that which is to be proved) is absent.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^63_106]: Upalabdhisahityaniyalama and sahopalambhaniyama are identical. The fallacy of anekanta vitiating this hetu was first exposed. Here it is shown that the inability to cite indirect proof applies to this, as it does to the other hetu, namely, niyamena ekajñānasiddhatvam.
\*The Benares edition reads vitti; the variant reading found in the Telugu edition and in some manuscripts has been preferred.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न चोपलब्धिसाहित्यनियमादेव तथात्वमत्रानुमेयमिति युक्तम्, विपक्षे बाधकानुपलब्धेः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

संविद्-अधीन-सिद्धितयापि तथा नियमोपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It may as well be that this invariable apprehension is due to objects depending for their manifestation on consciousness,
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

संविदधीनसिद्धितयापि तथा नियमोपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अनैन्द्रियिकत्वेन च तद्-वृत्ति-विपर्ययस्याकिञ्चित्करत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Since the reference to the deviation from the normal mode of working of the senses serves no purpose for the reason that (knowledge and knower) are not cognised by the senses, (you cannot point out that the perception of difference, like the perception of two moons, is due to the deviation from the normal mode of working of the senses).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनैन्द्रियिकत्वेन च तद्वृत्तिविपर्ययस्याकिञ्चित्करत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

योग्यानुपलम्भ-पराकृतत्वाच् च बाधक-प्रत्ययस्य ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

As the existence of a sublating cognition is denied by effectual non-perception, (the perception of difference cannot be declared to be false).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

योग्यानुपलम्भपराकृतत्वाच्च बाधकप्रत्ययस्य ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अपि च विषय-सिद्धिर् हि संवित् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Moreover, consciousness is well-known to be the manifestation of objects;[^63_107]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^63_107]: See note 104.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अपि च विषयसिद्धिर्हि संवित् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

सा च स्वयम्प्रकाशेत्य् अविवादः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

and that it is self-luminous is beyond dispute;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सा च स्वयम्प्रकाशेत्यविवादः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तेनावर्जनीयस्तथा नियमः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

hence, such an invariable manifestation of knowledge and the known is unavoidable.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तेनावर्जनीयस्तथा नियमः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च भेदो ऽपि सिद्धिम् अन्तरेण सिध्येद् इत्य् अनुन्मत्तेन युक्तम् आपादयितुम् इत्य् अलम् अनेनानुभव-पराहत-मतातिव्याकुलीकरणेन ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P64]] The contention that distinction (of objects from one another) can be established without the aid of consciousness is not likely to be put forward by any one who is not mad. Let this violent shaking of the doctrine which is opposed to experience suffice.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच भेदोऽपि सिद्धिमन्तरेण सिध्येदित्यनुन्मत्तेन युक्तमापादयितुमित्यलमनेनानुभवपराहतमतातिव्याकुलीकरणेन ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति सौगताभिमत-ग्राह्य-ग्राहक-विकल्प-प्रत्युद्धार-निराकरणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति सौगताभिमतग्राह्यग्राहकविकल्पप्रत्युद्धारनिराकरणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Refutation of the contention that there is no object that does not manifest itself-
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अप्रकाशात्मनश् च नीलादेः प्रकाश इत्य् अनुभव-सिद्धत्वान् न समर्थनान्तरं प्रार्थयते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Since the notion that the manifestation of objects, such as, blue and the like, which, in their nature, are not self-luminous, (is effected by consciousness) is vouched for by experience, it requires no other proof.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अप्रकाशात्मनश्च नीलादेः प्रकाश इत्यनुभवसिद्धत्वान्न समर्थनान्तरं प्रार्थयते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

आत्मा तु प्रकाश-स्वभाव एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The self, on the contrary, is essentially self-luminous.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

आत्मा तु प्रकाशस्वभाव एव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तावता ज्ञानत्वम्, स्वतन्त्रत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

On this count alone, the self cannot be knowledge, as the former is self-dependent.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच तावताज्ञानत्वम्, स्वतन्त्रत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

परतन्त्रम् आगन्तु यावद् अर्थेन्द्रियसन्निकर्षादिकारण-सन्निधानम् अवतिष्ठमानम् अर्थावच्छिन्न-रूपं ज्ञानम् इति प्रागेवावोचम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

It has already been stated that knowledge is dependent (on the self), that it is occasional, that it exists only so long as the causes, such as, the contact of the senses with their objects, persist, and that its nature is to pertain to some object or other.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

परतन्त्रमागन्तु यावदर्थेन्द्रियसन्निकर्षादिकारणसन्निधानमवतिष्ठमानमर्थावच्छिन्नरूपं ज्ञानमिति प्रागेवावोचाम ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

आत्मा तु स्वतन्त्रो ज्ञाता अहम् इति प्रत्यात्मं प्रथते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The self, on the contrary, is independent, and is the knowing subject; it shines as the 'I' in every self.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

आत्मा तु स्वतन्त्रो ज्ञाता अहमिति प्रत्यात्मं प्रथते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[यदिपुनरीदृशोऽप्ययमनन्याधीनसिद्धितया|यदि पुनर् ईदृशो ऽप्य् अयम् अनन्याधीन-सिद्धितया]] ज्ञानम् अभिलप्यते, अभिलप्यतां कामम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even when it is of this nature, if the self is termed knowledge, on the ground that it does not depend for its manifestation on something other than itself, you are welcome to say so.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदिपुनरीदृशोऽप्ययमनन्याधीनसिद्धितया ज्ञानमभिलप्यते, अभिलप्यतां कामम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथापि ज्ञान-वद् एव इदं ज्ञानम्, न ज्ञप्ति-मात्रतया ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even when it is so (described), surely, this knowledge is the possessor of knowledge, and not such a pure consciousness (as is held by you).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथापि ज्ञानवदेवेदं ज्ञानम्, न ज्ञप्तिमात्रतया ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इत्य् अद्वैताभिमत-ग्राह्य-ग्राहक-विकल्प-प्रत्युद्धार-निराकरणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इत्यद्वैत्यभिमतग्राह्यग्राहकविकल्पप्रत्युद्धारनिराकरणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इत्यद्वैत्यभिमतग्राह्यग्राहकविकल्पप्रत्युद्धारनिराकरणम्)
</details>

## आत्म-स्वरूपे शब्दः
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Scriptural support for the existence of a soul distinct from consciousness:
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अत एव हि च्छन्दोगाः ऽअथ यो वेदेदं जिघ्राणीति स आत्माऽ इत्य् आद्यामनन्ति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Indeed, for that very reason, the *Chandogas* (those who chant the Sama-veda) declare "He who has the awareness of 'let me smell this' he is the self."[^64_108]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^64_108]: *Chand*., *Up*. VII. xii.4.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अत एव हि च्छन्दोगाःऽअथ यो वेदेदं जिघ्राणीति स आत्माऽ इत्याद्यामनन्ति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा ऽकतम आत्माऽ इति प्रश्न-पूर्वकम् इदम् एव लक्षणम् आमनन्ति वाजसनेयिनः ऽयो ऽयं विज्ञानमयः प्राणेषु हृद्य् अन्तर्-ज्योतिः पुरुषःऽ इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Similarly, after the question "what is the soul?" has been raised, *Vajasaneyins* offer the same definition (of the soul, namely "He who is in the midst of the senses and vital breath, who has knowledge for his essence and who is the light inside the heart, he is the person,"[^64_109]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^64_109]: *Brh*. *Up*. IV. iii. 7.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाऽकतम आत्माऽ इति प्रश्नपूर्वकमिदमेव लक्षणमामनन्ति वाजसनेयिनःऽयोऽयं विज्ञानमयः प्राणेषु हृद्यन्तर्ज्योतिः पुरुषःऽ इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अत्र हि यो ऽयं सर्व-लोकानुभव-सिद्धो विविध-विषय-वेदन-प्रचुरः प्राणेषु प्रेरकतया स्थितो हृदयायतने अन्तर्-ज्योतिः अहम् इति प्रत्यक्त्वेन प्रकाशते, स पुरुष इति यथोदितम् एवात्म-स्वरूपम् उपदिश्यते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P65]] It is only in the manner indicated already that the true nature of the soul has been here described as follows - "He who is experienced by everybody, who is filled with knowledge concerning diverse objects, who resides among the senses and breath as their director, who is the inward light in the region of the heart, and who shines for his own sake as the 'I,' is the purusa."
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अत्र हि योऽयं सर्वलोकानुभवसिद्धो विविधविषयवेदनप्रचुरः प्राणेषु प्रेरकतया स्थितो हृदयायतने अन्तर्ज्योतिः अहमिति प्रत्यक्त्वेन प्रकाशते, स पुरुष इति यथोदितमेवात्मस्वरूपमुपदिश्यते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ऽएष हि द्रष्टा श्रोता घ्राता रसयिता मन्ता बोद्धा कर्ता विज्ञानात्मा पुरुषःऽ इत्य् आथर्वणाः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The followers of Atharva veda say "Truly, this entity; the seer, hearer, smeller, taster, thinker (mantr), knower (boddhr), doer (karta), he who has knowledge for his essence, is the purusa."[^65_110]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^65_110]: *Prasna*. Up. *IV.*
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ऽएष हि द्रष्टा श्रोता घ्राता रसयिता मन्ता बोद्धा कर्ता विज्ञानात्मा पुरुषःऽ इत्याथर्वणाः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा ऽविज्ञातारम् अरे केन विजानीयाद् इति ऽऽन पश्यो मृत्युं पश्यति न रोगं नोत दुःखताम् ऽऽस उत्तमः पुरुषः नोपजनं स्मरन्न् इदं शरीरम् ऽऽएवम् एवास्य परिदृष्टुरिमाः षोडशकलाः पुरुषायणाः पुरुषं प्राप्यास्तं गच्छन्ति ऽऽतस्माद् धा एतस्मान् मनोमयाद् अन्यो ऽन्तर आत्मा विज्ञानमयः ऽ इत्य् आद्याः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Similarly, the following and other passages are found :--- "Lo! whereby would one understand the understander?"[^65_111] "The seer sees neither death nor sickness, nor the evil in the world"[^65_112]; "He (the highest light to which the jiva reaches up) is the Supreme Person, ""The jiva experiences him in diverse ways. . . not thinking of the body cast behind in the midst of his kin"[^65_113] "Even so, the sixteen parts (kalas) of the experiencer (jiva), which depend (for their existence, nature and continuance) on the Highest Person, on reaching Him, become incapable of entangling Him in pleasure, pain, etc."[^65_114] "Different from that made of mind is another inner soul consisting of knowledge."[^65_115]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^65_111]: *Brh*. *Up*. *II*. iv. *14.*
[^65_112]: *Chand*. *Up*. *VII*. xxvi. 2
[^65_113]: *Chand*. *Up. VIII*. xii. 3
[^65_114]: *Prasna*. *Up*. V
[^65_115]: *Tait*. *Up.* II. 4.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ऽविज्ञातारमरे केन विजानीयादितिऽऽन पश्यो मृत्युं पश्यति न रोगं नोत दुःखताम्ऽऽस उत्तमः पुरुषः नोपजनं स्मरन्निदं शरीरम्ऽऽएवमेवास्य परिदृष्टुरिमाः षोडशकलाः पुरुषायणाः पुरुषं प्राप्यास्तं गच्छन्तिऽऽतस्माद्धा एतस्मान्मनोमयादन्योऽन्तर आत्मा विज्ञानमयःऽ इत्याद्याः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ऽसत्यं ज्ञानम् ऽ इत्य् अत्रापि ब्रह्म-लक्षण-निर्देशे ज्ञान-शब्दो न ज्ञान-मात्र-वचनः ; अपि तु तद्वद्-वचनः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even while defining Brahman, in the text-- Brahman is satya, jñāna 'the word jñāna does not refer to mere knowledge, but to the possessor of it;
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ऽसत्यं ज्ञानऽ मित्यत्रापि ब्रह्मलक्षणनिर्देशे ज्ञानशब्दो न ज्ञानमात्रवचनः ; अपि तु तद्वद्वचनः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तद्वचनत्वे ऽलिति ऽ इति आद्युदात्तत्व-प्रसक्तेः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

for, if it referred to the former, according to the sutra-liti[^65_116] it would follow that the first syllable must have the principal accent.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^65_116]: *Aṣṭādhyāyi*. *VI*. i. *193*
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तद्वचनत्वेऽलितिऽ इति आद्युदात्तत्वप्रसक्तेः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अन्तोदात्तश् चायं ज्ञान-शब्दः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

But this word, jñāna has its principal accent on the last syllable.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अन्तोदात्तश्चायं ज्ञानशब्दः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

मत्वर्थीयाच्-प्रत्ययान्तत्वे तथात्वं घटते; नान्यथेत्य् एतत्परमात्म-निरूपणे अतिनिपुणम् उपपादयिष्यामः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The word jñāna being so accented will be appropriate only if it has, at its termination, the suffix *ac*, which conveys the same meaning as the suffix *matup*. Otherwise, it would not be (appropriate). We shall explain this very clearly while treating of the Supreme Self.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

मत्वर्थीयाच्प्रत्ययान्तत्वे तथात्वं घटते; नान्यथेत्येतत्परमात्मनिरूपणे अतिनिपुणमुपपादयिष्यामः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ऐतरेयोपनिषद् अपि ऽप्रज्ञानं ब्रह्म ऽ इत्य् उक्त्वा ऽस एतेन प्राज्ञेनात्मना ऽ इति प्रकृष्ट-ज्ञान-वन्तम् एवेश्वरं दर्शयति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The Aitareya Upanisad also, after describing Brahman in the words 'prajñāna is Brahman', refers to the Lord as the possessor of supreme intelligence by the expression 'he (Vamadeva), by means of this Self possessed of intelligence.[^65_117]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^65_117]: *Ait*. *Up*. *Part* V.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ऐतरेयोपनिषदपिऽप्रज्ञानं ब्रह्येऽत्युक्त्वाऽस एतेन प्राज्ञेनात्मनाऽ इति प्रकृष्टज्ञानवन्तमेवेश्वरं दर्शयति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तत्-सिद्धं ज्ञातैवायम् आत्मेति ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Therefore, it is clear that this soul is truly the knower.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तत्सिद्धं ज्ञातैवायमात्मेति ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति देहादि-विलक्षण-प्रत्यगात्म-स्वरूप-निरूपण-प्रकरणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति देहादिविलक्षणप्रत्यगात्मस्वरूपनिरूपणप्रकरणम्)
</details>


## जीव-प्रमाणम्
<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

THE PRAMANA BY WHICH THE EXISTENCE OF THE JIVA IS ESTABLISHED
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

किं पुनर् अस्मिन् देहादि-व्यतिरेकिणि चेतने प्रत्यगात्मनि प्रमाणम्? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P66]] What is the means of knowledge (pramāņa) by which this individual self, which is distinct from the body and the like, and which is intelligent, is established?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

किं पुनरस्मिन्देहादिव्यतिरेकिणि चेतने प्रत्यगात्मनि प्रमाणम्? ।
</details>

### नैयायिकानुमानम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

(a) The Nyaya view that the soul is established through inference-
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[अनु मानमिति|अनुमानम् इति]] नय-विचक्षणो ऽक्षपादः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Akṣapāda, who is master of the science of logic, thinks that it is inference.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अनु मानमिति नयविचक्षणोऽक्षपादः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यद्-आह " इच्छा-द्वेष-प्रयत्न-सुख-दुःख-[[ज्ञाना न्यात्मनो|ज्ञानान्य् आत्मनो]] लिङ्ग [[लिङ्ग "म् इति|म्" इति]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

What he says is-"Desire, hate, pleasure, pain and knowledge are the reasons pointing to the existence of the soul."[^66_118]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^66_118]: Icchadvesaprayatnasukhajñānānyātmano liñāni *Nyāya*-*Sutra*, I. i. *10*
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यदाह " इच्छाद्वेषप्रयत्नसुखदुःखज्ञाना न्यात्मनो लिङ्ग "म् इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

किम् अमीषाम् आत्मनाविनाभावो धूमध्वज-विशेषेणेव धूम-विशेषस्य दृष्टः?
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Has invariable concomitance between these and the soul, like that between smoke and fire (dhūmadhvaja), been observed anywhere?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

किममीषामात्मनाविनाभावो धूमध्वजविशेषेणेव धूमविशेषस्य दृष्टः?
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

हन्तैवं तत एव तत्-प्रमितेः किम् अनुमानेन? ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Indeed, if so, as the knowledge of the self is obtained thence itself, what is the need for inference?
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

हन्तैवं तत एव तत्प्रमितेः किमनुमानेन? ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

मा भूद् विशेषतो दर्शनम्; सामान्यतस् तु भविष्यति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(The opponent replies) no invariable concomitance may have been observed in particular (between qualities such as desire, etc., and the soul); but, in general (i.e., between qualities and their substrate), it may be noticed.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

माभूद्विशेषतोदर्शनम्; सामान्यतस्तु भविष्यति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[तथाहिइच्छादयः|तथा हि — इच्छादयः]] कार्यत्वानित्यत्व-गुणत्वादिभिः शब्दादय इवाऽश्रिततयानुमीयन्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

To make the point clear... Desire and other qualities, like sound and so on, are inferred to be dependent upon something, for the reason of their being effects, non-eternal (entities) attributes, and so on.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिइच्छादयः कार्यत्वानित्यत्वगुणत्वादिभिः शब्दादय इवाऽश्रिततयानुमीयन्ते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यश् चैषाम् आश्रयः स आत्मा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That which is the substrate of these (qualities) is the self.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यश्चैषामाश्रयः स आत्मा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

गुणत्वं च परिशेषात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That desire and the like are qualities is inferred by elimination.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

गुणत्वं च परिशेषात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न सामान्य-विशेष-समवायाभावाः अनित्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Being non-eternal, they cannot be either generality *(sāmānya*), or particularity (*višeṣa*), or inherence (samavāya), or non-existence (abhāva).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न सामान्यविशेषसमवायाभावाः अनित्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न द्रव्यं कर्म वा, व्यापक-द्रव्य-समवायाद् इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

As they are inherent in all-pervasive substances, they cannot be either substance *(dravya*) or action (karma).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न द्रव्यं कर्म वा, व्यापकद्रव्यसमवायादिति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

विशेष-गुणत्वं च अनित्यत्वे सत्य् अस्मद्-आद्य् एकेन्द्रिय-[[ग्राह्यत्वनियमात्रूपादिवत्|ग्राह्यत्व-नियमाद् रूपादि-वत्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That they are specific qualities *(višeṣaguņa*) is established by the fact that at all times, like colour and other qualities, they, while being non-eternal, are grasped by one of our senses.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

विशेषगुणत्वं च अनित्यत्वे सत्यस्मदाद्येकेन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वनियमात्रूपादिवत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

After proving in general terms that consciousness, being a guņa, must have a substrate, it is shown by a process of elimination that it must be a specific entity, namely ātmā :—
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एवम् आश्रय-मात्रम् उपस्थापयन्तो ऽन्वय-व्यतिरेकिणो हेतवः द्रव्यान्तर-गुणत्वं च प्रत्याचक्षाणैः केवल-व्यतिरेकि-साधनैर् आत्म-गोचरतया नियम्यन्ते ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The reasons concomitant in affirmation and negation *(anvayavyatirekino hetavaḥ*), which, in this manner, indicate only (the need of) some substrate (for desire, etc.), are narrowed down in their scope in such a way as to refer to the soul by the reasons which are concomitant in negation only (*kevalavyatirekisādhanaiḥ*) and which disprove the view that they are qualities of substances other than the soul.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एवमाश्रयमात्रमुपस्थापयन्तोऽन्वयव्यतिरेकिणो हेतवः द्रव्यान्तरगुणत्वं च प्रत्याचक्षाणैः केवलव्यतिरेकिसाधनैरात्मगोचरतया नियम्यन्ते ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा हि [[भवतिइच्छादयो|भवति — इच्छादयो]] न महा-भूत-गुणाः, स्वात्मन एव प्रत्यक्षत्वात्; [[अबाह्येन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वाद्धा|अबाह्येन्द्रिय-ग्राह्यत्वाद् वा]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That this is so is evident from the following :- Desire and the like are not the qualities of the primal elements (mahābhūtas), because they are perceived only by oneself, or because they are not to be grasped by the outer senses.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथा हि भवतिइच्छादयो न महाभूतगुणाः, स्वात्मन एव प्रत्यक्षत्वात्; अबाह्येन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वाद्धा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ये भूत-गुणास् ते स्वात्म-परात्म-प्रत्यक्षाः बाह्य-करण-प्रत्यक्षाश् च, यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P67]] The qualities belonging to the primal elements, such as colour and the like, are perceivable by oneself and others and are perceived by the outer senses'; but desire and the like are not so (perceivable); hence, they are not the qualities of primal elements.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ये भूतगुणास्ते स्वात्मपरात्मप्रत्यक्षाः बाह्यकरणप्रत्यक्षाश्च, यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न तथेच्छादय इति न तद्-गुणाः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

but desire and the like are not so (perceivable); hence, they are not the qualities of primal elements.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न तथेच्छादय इति न तद्गुणाः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

दिक्-काल-मनांसि पुनः न विशेष-गुणवन्ति; नापि तद्-गुणानां प्रत्यक्षत्वम् इति न तेषामपि गुणाः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Again, space (dik), time and mind (manas) do not have specific qualities; and their attributes are not open to perception; hence, desire and the like are not their qualities.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

दिक्कालमनांसि पुनः न विशेषगुणवन्ति; नापि तद्गुणानां प्रत्यक्षत्वमिति न तेषामपि गुणाः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[अकारणगुणपूर्वत्वातयावच्छरीरभावित्वादित्यादयः|अकारणगुणपूर्वत्वाद् अयावच्छरीरभावित्वादित्यादयः]] शरीर-विशेष-गुणत्व-प्रतिषेध-हेतवः प्राचीनाश् चात्रानुक्रष्टव्याः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Reasons, such as the following---since they are not dependent on the causal substances; since they do not exist as long as the body lasts--(reasons) which were cited before, and which refute the view that they are specific qualities of the body, are to be brought forward and applied here also.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अकारणगुणपूर्वत्वातयावच्छरीरभावित्वादित्यादयः शरीरविशेषगुणत्वप्रतिषेधहेतवः प्राचीनाश्चात्रानुक्रष्टव्याः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तेनेच्छादयो न शरीर-गुणाः तद्-गुण-भावापवाद-प्रमाण-वत्त्वे सति गुणत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Therefore, desire and the like are not the qualities of the body; for, while there is evidence contradicting the view that they are the qualities of the body, they are qualities.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तेनेच्छादयो न शरीरगुणाः तद्गुणभावापवादप्रमाणवत्त्वे सति गुणत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

ये यथोक्त-साध्या न भवन्ति, ते यथोक्त-साधना अपि न भवन्ति; यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Whatever does not possess the sadhya does not have the aforesaid sadhana either, as in the case of colour.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

ये यथोक्तसाध्या न भवन्ति, ते यथोक्तसाधना अपि न भवन्ति; यथा रूपादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथोक्त-साधनाः पुनर् इच्छादय इति यथोक्त-साध्या एवेति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Desires and the like, however, possess the aforesaid hetu, and hence, they possess the sādhya.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथोक्तसाधनाः पुनरिच्छादय इति यथोक्तसाध्या एवेति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

विमति-पदास्पदेभ्यः [[शरीरादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणत्वप्रतिज्ञापि|शरीरादिभ्यो ऽर्थान्तर-गुणा]] इच्छादय इति वा प्रतिज्ञा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Or, the thesis to be proved (instead of being 'Desire and the like are not the qualities of the body') may be the following--Desire and the like are qualities of some substance other than the body, which is the point under dispute.[^67_119]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^67_119]: The point in dispute is not the existence of the body, but its possessing desires etc., as attributes.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

विमतिपदास्पदेभ्यः शरीरादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणा इच्छादय इति वा प्रतिज्ञा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

यथोक्त एव हेतुः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The aforesaid hetu and illustrative example may be cited (in the case of this thesis also).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

यथोक्त एव हेतुः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

उदाहरणं च प्रयोक्तव्यम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The aforesaid hetu and illustrative example may be cited (in the case of this thesis also).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

उदाहरणं च प्रयोक्तव्यम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

सामान्येन वा अन्वयः [[प्रदर्शनीयःयो|प्रदर्शनीयः — यो]] यद्-गुण-भावापवादक-प्रमाण-वत्त्वे सति गुणः, [[ततोर्ऽथान्तरस्य|स ततो ऽर्थान्तरस्य]] गुणः; यथा पृथिव्य् आदिभ्यः शब्द इति आकाश-सिद्धि-वद् आत्म-सिद्धिर् इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Positive concomitance too may be shown in a somewhat general way. That which is a quality, when there is evidence contradicting the view that it is the quality of a given entity, is the attribute of something other than that given entity, just as sound is the quality of something other than earth and the like. In this way, just as ether (ākāśa) is proved (to be the substrate of sound), the self is established (to be the substrate of desire and the like.)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सामान्येन वान्वयः प्रदर्शनीयःयो यद्गुणभावापवादकप्रमाणवत्त्वे सति गुणः, स ततोर्ऽथान्तरस्य गुणः; यथा पृथिव्यादिभ्यः शब्द इति आकाशसिद्धिवदात्मसिद्धिरिति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मन आनुमानिकत्व-पक्ष-निरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मन आनुमानिकत्वपक्षनिरूपणम्)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति विलक्षणात्मन आनुमानिकत्वपक्षनिरूपणम्)
</details>

#### खण्डनम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Refutation of the Nyaya view
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

इदमपि न समीचीनम् इत्य् एके ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Some consider that this (view) is not correct.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

इदमपि न समीचीनमित्येके ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[तथाहिअन्वयव्यतिरेकिहेतुभिर्देहादिसाधारणमाश्रयमात्रमवगमितम्|तथा हि — अन्वय-व्यतिरेकि-हेतुभिर् देहादि-साधारणम् आश्रय-मात्रम् अवगमितम्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

To elucidate this point,--with the aid of reasons concomitant in affirmation and negation *(anvayavyatireki*) it was only made known that there must be some support (for desire and other qualities), which might be either the body or some other substance.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथाहिअन्वयव्यतिरेकिहेतुभिर्देहादिसाधारणमाश्रयमात्रमवगमितम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च तावता ऽत्म-सिद्धिः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

By this reasoning alone the soul is not established (to be that substrate).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न च तावताऽत्मसिद्धिः ।
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

Argument from pure negative concomitance fares no better :—
</details>


<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

केवल-व्यतिरेकी तु साधन-दशाम् एव नासादयति, सपक्षान्वय-विरहात्, असाधारण-वत् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P68]] The reason concomitant in negation alone *(kevalavyatireki*) does not even possess the quality of being a correct reason; for, as in the fallacy called *asādhārana,* there is absence of the probans in instances where the sadhya is surely met with (sapaksa).[^68_120]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^68_120]: In the argument, sound is eternal, because it is sound the hetu is vitiated by the fallacy of asādhāreņa; for, it is not present in any sapaksa (i.c., similar examples where the sadhya is present) even as it is not present in the vipaksa. Similarly, in cases where reasons concomitant in negation alone (*kevalavyatireki*) are employed, there being no sapaksa, it is impossible to show the presence of the hetu in apaksas. Hence, *kevalavyatireki* is considered fallacious. It is defective for another reason also. In order to show that wherever the sadhya is absent the hetu is also absent the sadhya must first have been understood previously; but it is not met with anywhere. Hence, the Vedantins dismiss kevalavyatirkī as being faulty. Cf. 'sadhyābhāvo vipakse kathamiva viditaḥ tasya sadhyaprasiddheh' *Tattvamuktākaļāpa, Buddhisara*, verse 53. See also *Nyaya*-*Parisuddhi* (Memorial edition, pp. 66-75) and *Didhiti*. The *Vedanta* Paribhāṣā rejects *kevalānvayi* also, on the score that the kevalanvayi requires a sadhya which is present everywhere and such a sadhya is inadmissible on the theory that Brahman is nirguna.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

केवलव्यतिरेकी तु साधनदशामेव नासादयति, सपक्षान्वयविरहात्, असाधारणवत् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[नचैवं|न च एवम्]] केवलान्वयिनो विपक्ष-व्यतिरेक-दर्शन-विकलतया साधारण-वद् असाधनत्वम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The objection that on this admission, even the reason concomitant in affirmation alone cannot be considered as correct: for, as in the fallacy known as *sadharana*, there is the failure to show the absence of the reason in the counter-example (vipaksa)[^68_121]---(this objection) does not stand.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^68_121]: The opponent says 'In the argument the mountain has fire, because it is knowable', the hetu is defective *(sādhārṇa*), because it is not absent in the vipakṣa. Similarly, in arguments employing reasons concomitant in affirmation alone *(*kevalanvayi), there being no vipaksa, the absence of the hetu in the vipaksa cannot be cited. Hence, kevalānvayi also is a defective process of reasoning.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नचैवं केवलान्वयिनो विपक्षव्यतिरेकदर्शनविकलतया साधारणवदसाधनत्वम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[देशकालादिशङ्गितोपाधिविगमेप्यन्वयदर्शनेन|देश-कालादि-शङ्कितोपाधि-विगमे ऽप्य् अन्वय-दर्शनेन]] साध्यान्वित-स्वभावतया परिनिश्चितत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Since, even in the absence of suspected limiting conditions (upadhís), such as space, time and the like, the co-presence (of the hetu and the sadhya) is found, it is definitely ascertained that the hetu has the character of being connected with the sadhya.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

देशकालादिशङ्गितोपाधिविगमेप्यन्वयदर्शनेन साध्यान्वितस्वभावतया परिनिश्चितत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च साधनाभावे साध्याभाव-दर्शन-मात्रेण साध्यान्वित-स्वभावत्वं शक्यं निश्चेतुम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

From the mere observation of the absence of the sadhya when there is the absence of the hetu, it is not possible to ascertain that the hetu has the character of being connected with the sadhya.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच साधनाभावे साध्याभावदर्शनमात्रेण साध्यान्वितस्वभावत्वं शक्यं निश्चेतुम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अभावस्यानन्तदेशव्यापितयानवयवेन ग्रहणस्यैव दुष्करत्वात्, कलयाप्य् अन्यत्र-वृत्तौ सम्बन्धे नियमासम्भवात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P69]] As the non-existence of the sadhya is met with in innumerable places, it is impossible even to take note of them all exhaustively. If even in a single place the hetu were to be present in some manner, the universality of the connection cannot be maintained.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अभावस्यानन्तदेशव्यापितयानवयवेन ग्रहणस्यैव दुष्करत्वात्, कलयाप्यन्यत्रवृत्तौ सम्बन्धे नियमासम्भवात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[सन्देहग्रस्तत्वाच्चकिं|सन्देह-ग्रस्तत्वाच् च किम्]] साधनाभाव-प्रयुक्तः साध्याभावः, किं वा निमित्तान्तर-प्रयुक्त इति ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Besides, it is a matter for doubt whether the non-existence of the sadhya is due to the absence of the hetu or to some other cause.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

सन्देहग्रस्तत्वाच्चकिं साधनाभावप्रयुक्तः साध्याभावः, किं वा निमित्तान्तरप्रयुक्त इति ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[पृथिव्यादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणत्वप्रतिज्ञापि|पृथिव्यादिभ्यो ऽर्थान्तर-गुणत्व-प्रतिज्ञापि]] द्रव्यान्तराप्रसिद्धेर् अप्रसिद्ध-विशेषणा ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even the thesis (that desire and the like) are the qualities of some entity other than earth and the like may be charged with having an unproven attribute (aprasiddha-*viseṣaṇa*), for that other entity has not been proved.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

पृथिव्यादिभ्योर्ऽथान्तरगुणत्वप्रतिज्ञापि द्रव्यान्तराप्रसिद्धेरप्रसिद्धविशेषणा ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

(इति नैयायिकाभिमतात्मानुमान-निरासः)
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

(इति नैयायिकाभिमतात्मानुमाननिरासः)
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

(इति नैयायिकाभिमतात्मानुमाननिरासः)
</details>

### साङ्ख्यम् अनुमानम्

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

(b) The Sankhya View

The Sankhya mode of proof stands discredited for the same reasons :-
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एतेन साङ्ख्योदीरित-साधन-भेदा अप्य् अपोदिता वेदितव्याः सङ्घात-परार्थत्वादयः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

By the same reasoning, even the various reasons (such as collocations exist for the sake of others) are to be understood as having been set aside.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

एतेन साङ्ख्योदीरितसाधनभेदा अप्यपोदिता वेदितव्याः सङ्घातपरार्थत्वादयः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

तथा च तान् एव तावद् आदितो व्याकुर्महे
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Let us analyse them in the order of their presentation.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

तथा च तानेव तावदादितो व्याकुर्महे
</details>

<details><summary>विषयः</summary>

The Sankhya proofs for the existence of soul.
</details>



<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[सङ्गातपरार्थत्वात्र्रिगुणादिविपर्ययादधिष्ठानात्|सङ्घात-परार्थत्वात् त्रिगुणादि-विपर्ययाद् अधिष्ठानात्]] । पुरुषो ऽस्ति भोक्तृ-भावात् कैवल्यार्थं प्रवृत्तेश् च ॥
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>


"Since collocations exist for the sake of something other than themselves, since (in this other) there is the absence of the three gunas and the like, since there must be control (of these collocations), since there must be an experiencer, and since there is activity for securing aloofness (from --prakṛti), the soul exists."[^69_122]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^69_122]: *Sankhya*-*Kārikā*, verse 17.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

" सङ्गातपरार्थत्वात्र्रिगुणादिविपर्ययादधिष्ठानात् ।  
पुरुषोऽस्ति भोक्तृभावात्कैवल्यार्थं प्रवृत्तेश्च ॥ "
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

[[अयम्अर्थःदेहेन्द्रियादयः|अयम् अर्थः — देहेन्द्रियादयः]] परार्थाः [[सङ्गातत्वाच्छयनासनशरणादिवत्|सङ्घातत्वाच् छयनासन-शरणादि-वत्]] ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

This means--Being collocations, the body, the senses and so on, like a bed, a seat, a house, etc., exist for the sake of something other than themselves.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अयम्अर्थःदेहेन्द्रियादयः परार्थाः सङ्गातत्वाच्छयनासनशरणादिवत् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

प्रत्यक्षं च शरीरस्य सङ्घातत्वं, भूतानां च ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

The character of being a collocation attributed to the body and the primal elements is vouched for by perception.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

प्रत्यक्षं च शरीरस्य सङ्घातत्वं, भूतानां च ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

अव्यक्त-महद्-अहङ्कारेन्द्रियाणां च सुख-दुःख-मोहात्मतया तथात्वम् अनुमेयं तद्वद् एव ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

That the same character (of being a collocation) belongs to unmanifest prakṛti (avyakta), mahat, ahamkāra and the senses, as to the body and elements, is to be inferred from the fact that the former are of the nature of pleasure, misery and delusion.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

अव्यक्तमहदहङ्कारेन्द्रियाणां च सुखदुःखमोहात्मतया तथात्वमनुमेयं तद्वदेव ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न [[चेन्द्रियाणामाहङ्कारिकत्वस्याभ्युपेतस्य|चेन्द्रियाणाम् आहङ्कारिकत्वस्याभ्युपेतस्य]], [[साध्यन्त्वाभिमतपारार्थ्यधर्मस्य|साध्यत्वाभिमत-पारार्थ्य-धर्मस्य]] [[चासंहतपरार्थत्वस्यान्यथात्वापादनादुभयविशेषविरुद्धत्वं|चासंहत-परार्थत्वस्यान्यथात्वापादनाद् उभय-विशेष-विरुद्धत्वं]] हेतोः; अहङ्कारान्वय-व्यतिरेकानुविधानेन " देवा वैकारिकाः स्मृताः " इत्य् आद्यागम-बलेन प्रकाश-लाघव-गुणान्वयेन च वैकारिकाभिधान-सात्त्विकाहङ्कार-भेद-योनित्वस्येन्द्रियाणां प्रमाण-सिद्धस्य अपवादानुपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

[[P70]] (A possible objection is that) when the senses are admitted to be derived from ahamkara and when the meaning of what is accepted as the sadhya, namely, the quality of existing for the sake of another is the quality of existing for the sake of another which is itself not a collocation, the respective reasons for the above only prove the opposite, and hence, they are subject to the fallacy of *ubhaya-viseşaviruddha.*[^70_123] (The Sankhya replies) this objection cannot be raised. Since the presence or the absence of the senses is dependent respectively upon the presence or the absence of ahamkāra, since there is support of scriptural passage such as, "The senses are considered to proceed from ahamkara,"[^70_124] since there is contact of qualities, viz., brightness and lightness[^70_125] (with the senses), the fact that the senses have for their source that variety of ahamkāra wherein the sattva quality predominates and which is known as *vaikārika* is well supported by evidence; hence, it would be improper to deny this fact.
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^70_123]: It is interesting to note that this identical argument has been cited as an example of ubhayaviseşaviruddha (1. e. Dharmadharmyubhaya visēşaviruddha), by Kumārila Bhatta in his Sloka-Varttika Anumanapariccheda. sl. 105-7. The six varieties of viruddha-Dharmasvarūpabādha, Dharmaviseṣabadha, Dharmisvarupabādha, Dharmivišeṣabādha, Dharmadharmyu- bhayaviše şabadha-have, in later times, been reduced to one, since all of them, in the last resort, only prove the opposite of what is intended to be proved.
[^70_124]: *Vişnu* Purāna, I. ii.41.
[^70_125]: *Sankhya*-*Karika*, verse 13. Sattvam laghu prakasakamistam
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

न चेन्द्रियाणामाहङ्कारिकत्वस्याभ्युपेतस्य, साध्यन्त्वाभिमतपारार्थ्यधर्मस्य चासंहतपरार्थत्वस्यान्यथात्वापादनादुभयविशेषविरुद्धत्वं हेतोः; अहङ्कारान्वयव्यतिरेकानुविधानेन " देवा वैकारिकाः स्मृताः " इत्याद्यागमबलेन प्रकाशलाघवगुणान्वयेन च वैकारिकाभिधानसात्त्विकाहङ्कारभेदयोनित्वस्येन्द्रियाणां प्रमाणसिद्धस्यापवादानुपपत्तेः ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

आत्मनस् तु सङ्घातत्वे तस्यापि सङ्घातान्तरार्थतयानवस्थापत्त्या निष्प्रमाणकानेककल्पनाप्रसङ्गात्, अप्रयोजकत्वाच् च सङ्घातत्वस्य शेषित्वे, [[दृष्टान्तदृष्टाशेषधर्मोपस्थापनेऽअनुमानप्रामाण्य|दृष्टान्त-दृष्टाशेष-धर्मोपस्थापने ऽनुमान-प्रामाण्य]]स्यैवासम्भवापत्तेः तद्-असङ्घातत्वस्य चाप्रचाल्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

Even so, the belief that the self is not a collocation is unshakable, for the reason that (1) if the soul were itself a collocation as it would have to exist for the sake of another collocation, there would result an unending series, and, as a consequence, many things for which evidence is lacking would have to be assumed; (2) the quality of being a collocation is not responsible for an entity being a śeşi (i. e. one for whose sake others exist); and (3) inference itself would lose its validity, if also the qualities found in the illustrative examples are taken into consideration.[^70_126]
</details>

<details><summary>English - Notes</summary>

[^70_126]: Cf. yadi vivakṣitārthavyatirekeņa anumānasya avivakṣitamapi vişayaḥ, manvetasyām kalpaṇāyām sarvānumānam vyāhanyeta. Nyāya-Vārtika (Chowkamba edn. pp. 344-45). See also Nyayavārtikaṭālparyatīkā (Benares edn. p. 600).
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

आत्मनस्तु सङ्घातत्वे तस्यापि सङ्घातान्तरार्थतयानवस्थापत्त्या निष्प्रमाणकानेककल्पनाप्रसङ्गात्, अप्रयोजकत्वाच्च सङ्घातत्वस्य शेषित्वे, दृष्टान्तदृष्टाशेषधर्मोपस्थापनेऽअनुमानप्रामाण्य स्यैवासम्भवापत्तेः तदसङ्घातत्वस्य चाप्रचाल्यत्वात् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

न च प्रमाणान्तर-बलेनानाहङ्कारिकत्वसङ्घातान्तरार्थत्वयोर् बाधे ऽबाधितेन सङ्घात-परार्थत्वेनापि न भवितव्यम् ।
</details>

<details><summary>English</summary>

When the refutation of the statements-that the senses do not proceed from ahamkāra ; and that the body, senses and the like exist for the sake of other collocations--is effected on the strength of some evidence, it will not necessarily follow that even the facts of their being a collocation and of their existing for the sake of others, which are uncontradicted, should stand condemned.
</details>

<details><summary>मूलम्</summary>

नच प्रमाणान्तरबलेनानाहङ्कारिकत्वसङ्घातान्तरार्थत्वयोर्बाधेऽबाधितेन सङ्घातपरार्थत्वेनापि न भवितव्यम् ।
</details>

<details open><summary>विश्वास-प्रस्तुतिः</summary>

एवं च संहतत्व-व्यापकावरुद्धत्रैगुण्यादिरहितो ऽसंहत आत्मा सिद्धः ।
